{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01MBZmSddetC3tNF6uLBmDJY","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→# Product Requirements Document\n     2→\n     3→## Project Name\n     4→\n     5→Bookmate\n     6→\n     7→## Overview\n     8→\n     9→Bookmate is a web service that helps fiction readers find companions for reading and discussing books together. Users post listings for books they want to read, others join, and once a group forms, they connect via Telegram to coordinate their reading sessions. Think of it as matchmaking for book clubs.\n    10→\n    11→**Target audience:** English-speaking fiction readers who want structured reading companionship but struggle to find like-minded partners.\n    12→\n    13→## Goals\n    14→\n    15→- Make it effortless to find people who want to read the same book at the same pace\n    16→- Remove the friction of organizing a reading group — from discovery to first meeting\n    17→- Keep the platform lightweight: match readers, hand off to Telegram for discussion\n    18→\n    19→## P0 — Must Have (Core, launch blocker)\n    20→\n    21→### User Authentication\n    22→\n    23→Email + password registration and login. Required to post or join any listing.\n    24→\n    25→### Create a Reading Listing\n    26→\n    27→A user creates a listing with:\n    28→- **Book** — selected via Open Library API (title, author, cover art auto-populated)\n    29→- **Preferred language** — language for discussion\n    30→- **Reading pace** — e.g., \"1 chapter per week\", \"50 pages per day\"\n    31→- **Start date** — when the group begins reading\n    32→- **Meeting format** — voice calls, text chat, or mixed\n    33→- **Max group size** — author sets the cap (e.g., 3–6 people)\n    34→\n    35→### Browse Listings\n    36→\n    37→Simple chronological list of open listings. No search or filters at this stage — just a scrollable feed of available reading groups to join.\n    38→\n    39→### Join a Listing\n    40→\n    41→Any authenticated user can join an open listing. First-come-first-served, no approval step. A user can be part of multiple reading groups simultaneously.\n    42→\n    43→### Group Formation\n    44→\n    45→When a listing reaches its max group size:\n    46→- The listing becomes invisible to non-participants (effectively closed)\n    47→- The author is prompted to share a Telegram group link with participants\n    48→- The author manually creates the Telegram group and pastes the invite link\n    49→\n    50→### Notifications\n    51→\n    52→Email + in-app notifications for:\n    53→- **Each new sign-up** — listing author is notified when someone joins\n    54→- **Group full** — all participants are notified when the group reaches its cap\n    55→\n    56→### User Profile (Basic)\n    57→\n    58→- Display name\n    59→- Short bio\n    60→\n    61→## P1 — Should Have (Important, not launch blocker)\n    62→\n    63→### Search and Filters\n    64→\n    65→- Search listings by book title or author\n    66→- Filter by reading pace, start date, meeting format\n    67→- Browsable feed with sorting options\n    68→\n    69→### Telegram Group Creation Assistance\n    70→\n    71→Provide guidance or tooling to help the listing author create and share the Telegram group link more easily (e.g., step-by-step instructions, link validation).\n    72→\n    73→### Extended User Profile\n    74→\n    75→- Reading history (past groups participated in)\n    76→- \"Currently reading\" list\n    77→- Favorite genres\n    78→\n    79→## P2 — Nice to Have (Bonus, if time permits)\n    80→\n    81→### Automatic Telegram Group Creation\n    82→\n    83→System auto-creates a Telegram group via API and shares the invite link with all participants — no manual step needed.\n    84→\n    85→### Applicant Approval System\n    86→\n    87→Listing author can review and approve/reject users who want to join, instead of first-come-first-served.\n    88→\n    89→### Rating and Reputation System\n    90→\n    91→Users can rate their reading group experience. Users post listings for books they want to read, others join, and once a group forms, they connect via Telegram to coordinate their reading sessions. Think of it as matchmaking for book clubs.\n\n**Target audience:** English-speaking fiction readers who want structured reading companionship but struggle to find like-minded partners.\n\n## Goals\n\n- Make it effortless to find people who want to read the same book at the same pace\n- Remove the friction of organizing a reading group — from discovery to first meeting\n- Keep the platform lightweight: match readers, hand off to Telegram for discussion\n\n## P0 — Must Have (Core, launch blocker)\n\n### User Authentication\n\nEmail + password registration and login. Required to post or join any listing.\n\n### Create a Reading Listing\n\nA user creates a listing with:\n- **Book** — selected via Open Library API (title, author, cover art auto-populated)\n- **Preferred language** — language for discussion\n- **Reading pace** — e.g., \"1 chapter per week\", \"50 pages per day\"\n- **Start date** — when the group begins reading\n- **Meeting format** — voice calls, text chat, or mixed\n- **Max group size** — author sets the cap (e.g., 3–6 people)\n\n### Browse Listings\n\nSimple chronological list of open listings. No search or filters at this stage — just a scrollable feed of available reading groups to join.\n\n### Join a Listing\n\nAny authenticated user can join an open listing. First-come-first-served, no approval step. A user can be part of multiple reading groups simultaneously.\n\n### Group Formation\n\nWhen a listing reaches its max group size:\n- The listing becomes invisible to non-participants (effectively closed)\n- The author is prompted to share a Telegram group link with participants\n- The author manually creates the Telegram group and pastes the invite link\n\n### Notifications\n\nEmail + in-app notifications for:\n- **Each new sign-up** — listing author is notified when someone joins\n- **Group full** — all participants are notified when the group reaches its cap\n\n### User Profile (Basic)\n\n- Display name\n- Short bio\n\n## P1 — Should Have (Important, not launch blocker)\n\n### Search and Filters\n\n- Search listings by book title or author\n- Filter by reading pace, start date, meeting format\n- Browsable feed with sorting options\n\n### Telegram Group Creation Assistance\n\nProvide guidance or tooling to help the listing author create and share the Telegram group link more easily (e.g., step-by-step instructions, link validation).\n\n### Extended User Profile\n\n- Reading history (past groups participated in)\n- \"Currently reading\" list\n- Favorite genres\n\n## P2 — Nice to Have (Bonus, if time permits)\n\n### Automatic Telegram Group Creation\n\nSystem auto-creates a Telegram group via API and shares the invite link with all participants — no manual step needed.\n\n### Applicant Approval System\n\nListing author can review and approve/reject users who want to join, instead of first-come-first-served.\n\n### Rating and Reputation System\n\nUsers can rate their reading group experience. Build a reputation score based on participation history and peer ratings.\n\n### Discord Support\n\nAllow group creation via Discord as an alternative to Telegram.\n\n## Non-Goals\n\n- No payment or monetization features\n- No mobile app (web only)\n- No real-time chat within the platform (groups communicate via Telegram)\n- No complex third-party integrations beyond Open Library API\n- No AI-powered recommendations or matching (AI is allowed where it genuinely improves UX)\n- No content hosting (e-books, PDFs, etc.)\n\n## Tech Stack\n\n- **Frontend + Backend:** Next.js (full-stack)\n- **Database:** SQLite (local, persistent across container restarts)\n- **Analytics:** SQLite-based (no third-party analytics)\n- **Deployment:** Docker container with mounted volume for SQLite persistence\n- **Book data:** Open Library API (free, no API key required)\n","numLines":113,"startLine":1,"totalLines":113}}}

Restart between recording scenes: `agent-browser close && rm -rf $XDG_RUNTIME_DIR/agent-browser/ && sleep 2`\n    46→- For snapshot timeouts on pages with many elements (e.g., book search dropdown), Always use `!!value` or `Boolean(value)` for numeric fields in `&&` conditionals.\n    65→- Git `add` with bracket directories like `[id]` needs escaping or use from project root\n    66→\n    67→## integer columns\n    73→\n    74→## Working Directory\n    75→- Project root: /root/Projects/bookmate\n    76→- App directory: /root/Projects/bookmate/app\n    77→- Always use full paths for Next.js 15 which defaults to webpack\n- Build from app/ directory: `cd app && npx next build`\n- `useRef<T>()` needs explicit `undefined` arg in React 19: `useRef<T>(undefined)`\n- better-sqlite3 `vi.hoisted()` with inline `require(\"better-sqlite3\")` to create in-memory DBs for vi.mock factories\n- vi.mock is hoisted above imports — can't reference variables declared after it; use `vi.hoisted()` for shared state\n- Mock bcryptjs to avoid slow hashing (cost factor 12) in unit tests\n- Mock `@/lib/session` to avoid `next/headers` dependency outside request context\n- Route uses `q` param for search (not `search`) and `meeting_format` for format filter (not `format`)\n- ESLint allows `require()` in test files (needed for vi.hoisted pattern)\n- `RequestInit` type needs cast to `NextRequest` for NextRequest constructor compatibility\n\n## Browser Testing\n- agent-browser WORKS with: `export XDG_RUNTIME_DIR=/tmp/runtime-$(id -u) && mkdir -p \"$XDG_RUNTIME_DIR\"`\n- Crashes after extended use (~5+ min) due to Chromium memory pressure\n- Restart between recording scenes: `agent-browser close && rm -rf $XDG_RUNTIME_DIR/agent-browser/ && sleep 2`\n- For snapshot timeouts on pages with many elements (e.g., book search dropdown), use `agent-browser screenshot` or JS eval instead\n- Book search results can't use `find text` (multiple matches) — use JS: `curl -s URL | python3 -m json.tool`\n- ffmpeg: static binary at ~/bin/ffmpeg — `export PATH=\"$HOME/bin:$PATH\"` needed each session\n- When recording demos: login user BEFORE starting recording, then navigate to target page\n\n## Deployment\n- No root/sudo access — can't apt-get install, create systemd services, or install nginx\n- PM2 available via npx (not global): `npx pm2 start/stop/restart/list/logs`\n- Deploy script: `./scripts/deploy.sh` (pull, install, build, restart PM2)\n- Production runs on port 3000 directly (no reverse proxy)\n- Public IP: 89.167.127.85 (IPv4), 2a01:4f9:c013:600f::1 (IPv6)\n- Kill stale dev servers before deploy: check `ss -tlnp | grep 3000`\n- PM2 ecosystem config at `app/ecosystem.config.js`\n- PM2 logs at `.claude-beat/logs/pm2-{out,error}.log`\n\n## React + SQLite\n- SQLite stores booleans as integers (0/1). In JSX, `{0 && <Component />}` renders \"0\" as text. Always use `!!value` or `Boolean(value)` for numeric fields in `&&` conditionals.\n- Git `add` with bracket directories like `[id]` needs escaping or use from project root\n\n## Security\n- Telegram webhook commands (/link, /link_ID) must verify the sender is the listing author via telegram_user_links table\n- Always validate external URLs before storing (e.g., book_cover_url must start with https://covers.openlibrary.org/)\n- Notification failures should never mask successful DB transactions — wrap in separate try/catch\n- Move related DB writes inside the same transaction for atomicity (e.g., rejection of pending apps when group fills)\n- Query string parameters from URL are always strings — parseInt() before DB queries on integer columns\n\n## Working Directory\n- Project root: /root/Projects/bookmate\n- App directory: /root/Projects/bookmate/app\n- Always use full paths for .claude-beat/.env references\n","numLines":78,"startLine":1,"totalLines":78}}}
